    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer236601950953821191">Children can have a cruel, absolute sense of justice. Children can kill a monster and feel quite proud of themselves.   <span id="freeText236601950953821191" style="display:none">Children can have a cruel, absolute sense of justice. Children can kill a monster and feel quite proud of themselves. A girl can look at her brother and believe they’re destined to be a knight and a bard who battle evil. She can believe she’s found the thing she’s been made for.<br /><br />Hazel lives with her brother, Ben, in the strange town of Fairfold where humans and fae exist side by side. The faeries’ seemingly harmless magic attracts tourists, but Hazel knows how dangerous they can be, and she knows how to stop them. Or she did, once.<br /><br />At the center of it all, there is a glass coffin in the woods. It rests right on the ground and in it sleeps a boy with horns on his head and ears as pointed as knives. Hazel and Ben were both in love with him as children. The boy has slept there for generations, never waking.<br /><br />Until one day, he does…<br /><br />As the world turns upside down, Hazel tries to remember her years pretending to be a knight. But swept up in new love, shifting loyalties, and the fresh sting of betrayal, will it be enough?</span>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/389356-i-know-they-hinted-at-it-but-who-is">I know they hinted at it, but who is Jack&#39;s father? I never really got it.</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_389356'><a id="like_count_community_question_389356" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/389356?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">5 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F20958632-the-darkest-part-of-the-forest">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/389356-i-know-they-hinted-at-it-but-who-is">5 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/389356-i-know-they-hinted-at-it-but-who-is">See all 8 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/58470325-julia-waters"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1479462430i/58470325._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/58470325-julia-waters">Julia Waters</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    Pretty sure it was the Alderking. Since he vowed to kill his next child, Eolanthe probably lied about having a mortal lover and hid Jack with the Gord<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    Pretty sure it was the Alderking. Since he vowed to kill his next child, Eolanthe probably lied about having a mortal lover and hid Jack with the Gordon family to protect him from the king. Obviously the "mortal lover" was not Mr. Gordon, so it wouldn't make sense to just never even hint at who the mortal father would have been. Also, there's the whole thing about Jack being an heir - can't be an heir with a mortal father. As far as the hint that Severin is familiar with Eolanthe, that would be explained if she was his father's longtime mistress. Severin is clever enough to have figured out that Eolanthe would consider herself too superior to have a mortal lover, and probably put two and two together, eventually realizing that Jack is his brother. Severin couldn't have been the father because he was asleep for hundreds of years prior to Jack's birth. <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>
</div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2027215053" />
    <a title="chai ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42130592-chai"><img alt="chai ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603167303p2/42130592.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2027215053?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chai ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chai ♡" href="/user/show/42130592-chai">chai ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=ya-sff">ya-sff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=trope-idiots-in-love">trope-idiots-in-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=trope-mortal-immortal">trope-mortal-immortal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=lgbtq-rep-side">lgbtq-rep-side</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=poc-rep">poc-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=trope-found-family">trope-found-family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=trope-gay-yearning">trope-gay-yearning</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2027215053" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17402036463216539823">I feel like my life is just a constant cycle of finally getting past the book I was obsessing about and then immediately finding another book to obsess about.<br/><br/>My heart is growing a lot and I want to cover this story and these characters in it. This book made me want to lie down on the forest floor for a moment or two and just breathe in and out and in and out, letting nature wash over me with dirt in my hair and dew on my skin while the sun slowly slips into the sky and the morning is slowly born</span>
  <span id="freeText17402036463216539823" style="display:none">I feel like my life is just a constant cycle of finally getting past the book I was obsessing about and then immediately finding another book to obsess about.<br /><br />My heart is growing a lot and I want to cover this story and these characters in it. This book made me want to lie down on the forest floor for a moment or two and just breathe in and out and in and out, letting nature wash over me with dirt in my hair and dew on my skin while the sun slowly slips into the sky and the morning is slowly borning all around me. I'm honestly a total fucking mess over this book.... but like, a glittery, light pink, soft mess. And I seriously wish it didn't have to end. I need at least five books starring these characters!<br /><br /><blockquote>🌟<b><u>so what is this book about?</u></b></blockquote><br /><br />The Darkest Part of The Forest is a standalone urban fantasy about two siblings - Hazel &amp; Ben, who live in a weird small town that borders a kingdom of fae and elves and all kinds of mythical creatures. And in the woods, there is a glass coffin and in it sleeps a horned beautiful elf prince.<br /><br />Hazel &amp; Ben - a forest fire and a gentle breeze, having too much earth and freedom in their hearts spent their childhood walking on the wild side, chasing cryptids and bad ideas (Hazel with a sword and Ben with hypnotizing music). That is, when they're not lying on the glass coffin, making up stories about the horned boy who's asleep beneath.....<b>until he disappears overnight.</b><br /><br /><blockquote><i>There’s a monster in our wood. She’ll get you if you’re not good. Drag you under leaves and sticks. Punish you for all your tricks. A nest of hair and gnawed bone. You are never, ever coming… home</i>.</blockquote><br /><br />This book has such winter vibes to it, the equivalent of waking up in the middle of the crispy night and looking out the window and there’s snow on the ground and the sky is kind of light-colored and it looks foggy and misplaced and kind of eerie but also comforting. And I honestly cannot believe there was ever a time when I didn’t have immediate access to this story. Actually, I've decided I'm completely disenchanted with the human experience and I'd like to retreat into this book!<br /><br /><blockquote>🌟<b><u>THE CHARACTERS:</u></b></blockquote><br /><br />One of the many things I loved about this book is the <strong>diversity</strong>. There are main characters of color and main queer characters whose storyline does not necessarily involve around their sexuality and I was so there for it!<br /><br />Also, this is basically <strong>a gay fairytale where the BOY GETS THE PRINCE </strong>and if that does not make you want to read this book immediately, I don't know what will...<br /><br />💫 <b>HAZEL</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Once, there was a girl who vowed she would save everyone in the world, but forgot herself.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />I wish a knight in shining armor would come and sweep me off my feet and by knight in shining armor I mean Hazel.<br /><br />Hazel unwittingly lives a double life. <em>Day</em> Hazel is an ordinary high school student who kisses too many boys to fill her empty. <em>Night</em> Hazel is the trusted and cunning knight whispering intrigues and rumors into the ear of the Alderking who then listens and adapts his court strategy to fit her given information. And one of them doesn't know the other one exists.<br /><br />I really love confident female characters and how they beam lighthouse just from arriving; those who are so inherently inspiring. I am forever proud of the characters who go from being fragile and incertain to confident and strong. Hazel has assigned herself the role of the knight in the story of her life. She's the one who forges the sword, charges into the woods and does the saving and I literally love her so much!!!!<br /><br />💫<b> BENJAMIN</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <br />
    <div>
      I need to stop fantasizing about running away to some other life and start figuring out the one I have.
    </div>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />OKAY. I seriously wish I had big soft wings to protect Benjamin so this is a public announcement that I'm hereby destroying the idea that any harm would ever come his way!<br /><br />Ben is a musician and that was a gift given to him by the Fae. Except, that gift came with a price and Benjamin has spent his entire life building a scaffolding of excuses to avoid admitting that the price was losing control.<br /><br />I really just love Ben so much!! He's so precious and I'm so glad he fell in love with someone who never stops choosing him and makes him feel at home when he look at them and aaah I'm literally ready to invest my entire livelihood just shipping him and Severin!!<br /><br />💫 <b>SEVERIN</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>We love until we do not. <em>F</em><i>or us, love doesn’t fade gradually. It snaps like a branch bent too far.</i></i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Don’t believe any boy who says “I’m not like other guys" unless he has curving horns, glowing green eyes and has been asleep in a glass coffin for generations. And only if he also happens to be <em>an elf prince</em>.<br /><br />Severin is the kind of character who would break a poet's heart and they’ll write poems about him forever and he will be on their wiki page as a mysterious, possibly villified figure. Everything about him is so iconic, from his glass coffin to the fact that he's a deadly elf prince but also just a goofy boy who spins in a swivel chair wearing his boyfriend's sweater.<br /><br />I honestly love Severin so much and I would actually like to be him. So I would really appreciate it if someone would make arrangements to sponsor my retreat into a desolate wilderness environment and my loved ones could only undergo the trek to come visit me exactly once a year on the winter solstice thanks.<br /><br />💫<b>JACK</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <br />
    <div>
      Well fine, then. I could send you out to win my favor. Possibly on a quest involving bringing a large mug of coffee and a doughnut. Or the wholesale slaughter of all my enemies. I haven’t decided which.
    </div>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Do yo ever think about a certain fictional character and your stomach just does the ✨ 💫 💖 🌟 💫 💫 🌈 ✨ 🌟 💖 💫 ✨ 🌈 thing? That's how I feel about Jack.<br /><br />Jack is a fae changeling who's been raised by a human family and he's become so good at tricking himelf out of remembering that he was not one of them, ignoring the holes in him that belonged to the other side of the border, the parts of him that don’t mesh well with this newfound world.... until the townsfolk were being attacked by the fae and the lingering blame fell on him. So which side is he going to fight for? (also, I'm here to ship him with Hazel with all my heart WHY ARE THEY ALL SO PRECIOUS I ONLY HAVE ONE HEART TO WORK WITH HERE!!!)<br /><br /><blockquote>🌟<u><b> OVERALL:</b></u></blockquote><br /><br />*me yelling from a megaphone on the street corner and handing out pamphlets* THE MORAL OF THIS STORY KIDS IS THAT Y'ALL ARE SLEEPING ON THIS BOOK AND YOU NEED TO READ IT ASAP!!<br /><br />Oh by the way, Benjamin &amp; Severin are playing the cameo role in Holly Black's new upcoming release <strong>The Cruel Prince </strong>so you really do want to read this book and meet them first!!<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <br />
    <div>
      I love you like in the storybooks. I love you like in the ballads. I love you like a lightning bolt. I’ve loved you since the third month you came and spoke with me. I loved that you made me want to laugh. I loved the way you were kind and the way you would pause when you spoke, as though you were waiting for me to answer you. I love you and I am mocking no one when I kiss you, no one at all.
    </div>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><a href="https://runawaywithdreamthieves.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">BLOG</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/kzabrekker" rel="nofollow noopener">TWITTER</a> | <a href="https://instagram.com/runawaywithdreamthieves" rel="nofollow noopener">INSTAGRAM</a> | <a href="https://azqaban.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">TUMBLR</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17402036463216539823" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2313407027" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2313407027" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2313407027?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=us-ya">us-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=ya-series">ya-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2313407027" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15351647628421777844">4.5 stars<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1566620168i/28042710._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/> <b>Holly Black at her finest.</b> <blockquote>
  <i>Once, there was a girl who vowed she would save everyone in the world, but forgot herself.</i>
</blockquote> Seriously, how does Holly Black create such<b> bone-chillingly wondrous books </b> time and time again?<br/><br/>Hazel Evans and her brother (Ben) live in Fairfold - a<b> town blessed (cursed?) by the fair folk.</b> The food tastes better, the art is more beautiful and <b>the world, far crueler. </b><blockquote>
  <i>There's a monster in our wood. <br/>She'll get you if you're not good.<br/> Drag you under leaves and st</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText15351647628421777844" style="display:none">4.5 stars<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1566620168i/28042710._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br> <b>Holly Black at her finest.</b> <blockquote>
  <i>Once, there was a girl who vowed she would save everyone in the world, but forgot herself.</i>
</blockquote> Seriously, how does Holly Black create such<b> bone-chillingly wondrous books </b> time and time again?<br><br>Hazel Evans and her brother (Ben) live in Fairfold - a<b> town blessed (cursed?) by the fair folk.</b> The food tastes better, the art is more beautiful and <b>the world, far crueler. </b><blockquote>
  <i>There's a monster in our wood. <br>She'll get you if you're not good.<br> Drag you under leaves and sticks. <br>Punish you for all your tricks. A<br>nest of hair and gnawed bone. <br>You are never, ever coming...</i>
</blockquote>And despite all that,<b> Hazel loves Fairfold</b> with every fiber of her being. Despite its wild and twisted ways,<b> Fairfold's magic has swept her up</b> and into its clutches...<blockquote>
  <i>Down a path worn into the woods, past a stream and a hollowed-out log full of pill bugs and termites, was a glass coffin. </i>
</blockquote> The town is famous (in part) due to the <b>horned boy with pointed ears</b> in the glass coffin. Generations have played on and around his coffin but the boy has <b>never aged and never moved. <i>Until now</i></b><br><br>The Horned Boy is no longer in the coffin. Quickly, Hazel realizes that her once (semi) safe town is in jeopardy and it is on her shoulders to keep the town safe. <b>
  <i>No matter what. </i>
</b><br><br>I love everything that Holly Black has ever written - the way <b>she breaths life into a book</b> just blows me away (and this book was no exception!). <br><br>The <b>cast of characters</b> really made this one shine. I admired Hazel's strength, Ben's devotion, Jack's otherworldly tendencies and Carter's love. The way they played off of each other was superb.<br><br>Also, I love the way Holly Black portrays LGBT characters in her books - they are never the main motive of the plot. They simply exist and the plot moves around them <b>(can I get a hallelujah!?) </b><br><br>Also, the story of Jack's origins just melted my heart. He needs his own book. Right. Now.<br><br>In short -<b> this one was fabulous. </b>I have a feeling that I'll be going for another reread in the near-future.<br><br><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br>Lauren Fortgang absolutely nails this narration. I just loved listening to her voice. Could not recommend this audiobook more.<br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4927959087123962645">I LOVED THE CHARACTERS in this!! If anything they were the pull that kept me coming back to this book. I also liked how weird this book got! BRING ON THE WEIRDNESS AND YOU'RE SURE TO WIN ME OVER. I do think this book missed the WOW factor and I wasn't super keen on the plot, but it was still a fun time.</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1047711974" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5636807575352924533"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567530468i/28094128._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>[September 20th, 2019]:</b> <br/>The Darkest Part of the Forest is still a masterpiece in 2019, and I'm honestly overwhelmed with how much I love this story.<br/><br/>I read this for <a href='https://youtu.be/uUQ5Uak2ivs' rel='nofollow noopener'>#FaerieAThon</a>, which I cohosted with <a href='https://www.youtube.com/user/janelindsey12' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jane</a>, <a href='https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCZVWupMY1F8SEsALG5ohE5Q' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kristin</a>, & <a href='https://www.youtube.com/user/alexalovesbooks' rel='nofollow noopener'>Alexa</a>! ❤<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1558814250i/27571200._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>[October 20th, 2015]:</b><br/><i>“Once, there was a girl who vowed she would save everyone in the world, but forgot herself.” </i><br/><br/>This was such a whimsical and beautiful story about a sleepy little down named Fairfold, who has a pact with all the faeries that if the fae leave them alone, al</span>
  <span id="freeText5636807575352924533" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567530468i/28094128._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>[September 20th, 2019]:</b> <br>The Darkest Part of the Forest is still a masterpiece in 2019, and I'm honestly overwhelmed with how much I love this story.<br><br>I read this for <a href="https://youtu.be/uUQ5Uak2ivs" rel="nofollow noopener">#FaerieAThon</a>, which I cohosted with <a href="https://www.youtube.com/user/janelindsey12" rel="nofollow noopener">Jane</a>, <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCZVWupMY1F8SEsALG5ohE5Q" rel="nofollow noopener">Kristin</a>, &amp; <a href="https://www.youtube.com/user/alexalovesbooks" rel="nofollow noopener">Alexa</a>! ❤<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1558814250i/27571200._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>[October 20th, 2015]:</b><br><i>“Once, there was a girl who vowed she would save everyone in the world, but forgot herself.” </i><br><br>This was such a whimsical and beautiful story about a sleepy little down named Fairfold, who has a pact with all the faeries that if the fae leave them alone, all the tourists are free game. But why would tourists want to visit this little town nestled in the forest? Oh, because a handsome horned fae boy is asleep in an unbreakable glass casket. Some visit because they do not believe in magic, some come because they do. Regardless of their beliefs or opinions, the tourists come. <br><br>The main character, Hazel, is a brave girl who tries to fight the evil fae with her brother. After a close scare, she makes a deal with the fae king of the forest for her brother to have his wish come true <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Her brother was blessed by a nice fae when he was young. He has a magical gift for music, but no means to hone that gift at a school far away from Fairfold. Hazel's deal allows him to go to music school on a full scholarship <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. She only had to trade seven years of her life that the king decides to take while she is asleep. So every night, Hazel does the king's bidding and wakes up in the morning, in her own bed, with no recollection on the night's events. Hazel is none the wiser, until the handsome horned fae boy is finally broken free of this glass casket. <br><br>One thing that kept sticking out to me was that there is a lot of "duos" in this book. For starters, it seems like each family has two children (Hazel/Ben, Jack/Carter, Severin/Sorrel). There are two side by side romances going on throughout the book (one f/m, one m/m). Both are wonderful, and leave you wanting more. Then a main story line is all about two powerful swords. Lastly, we are also given night Hazel verses day Hazel. There is lots of coupling and pairs throughout this impactful little story.<br><br><i>“We love until we do not. For us, love doesn't fade gradually. It snaps like a branch bent too far.” </i><br><br>I can't say too much more without giving away some amazing twists and turns, but this was such a good read. This is exactly the kind of fantasy book I like to read. This spoke to my heart and soul, and I enjoyed it immensely. Holly Black is such a wonderful writer, and her art of threading words together that will make you feel everything under the sun, is untouchable. I have loved and devoured everything she's ever written, and The Darkest Part of the Forest was no exception.<br><br><i>“I love like in the storybooks. I love you like in the ballads. I love you like a lightning bolt. I've loved you since the third month you came and spoke with me. I loved that you made me want to laugh. I loved the way you were kind and the way you would pause when you spoke, as though you were waiting for me to answer you. I love you and I am mocking no one when I kiss you, no one at all.” </i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445548897i/16669114._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I was also lucky enough to get this signed from B&amp;N when it was first released this year. <br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1152990035" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1152990035" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1152990035?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fairies">fairies</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1152990035" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9558718422290167570"><strong>
  <em>Down a path worn into the woods, past a stream and a hollowed-out log full of pill bugs and termites, was a glass of coffin. It rested right on the ground and in it slept a boy with horns on his head and ears as pointed as knives.</em>
</strong><br/><br/>*<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25422.Holly_Black' title='Holly Black' rel='nofollow noopener'>Holly Black</a> has written a considerable amount of books, but this is the first novel by her that I have read. Not that I was not interested in the others: I am simply always too excited by new releases. While wondering what great reads 2015 would bring us, I found t</span>
  <span id="freeText9558718422290167570" style="display:none"><strong>
  <em>Down a path worn into the woods, past a stream and a hollowed-out log full of pill bugs and termites, was a glass of coffin. It rested right on the ground and in it slept a boy with horns on his head and ears as pointed as knives.</em>
</strong><br /><br />*<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25422.Holly_Black" title="Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">Holly Black</a> has written a considerable amount of books, but this is the first novel by her that I have read. Not that I was not interested in the others: I am simply always too excited by new releases. While wondering what great reads 2015 would bring us, I found this and immediately felt pulled toward it.<br /><br />The book started with a fairytale-like atmosphere. I thought the storytelling was delightful and only wished to read more and more. Admittedly, it is, along with the world-building, what held my interest at first, really, for the main character did not manifest the type of personality I generally enjoy reading about. We had very little in common. For instance, she attended parties, kissed boy after boy and that with no real remorse or noticeable emotions after breaking their heart.<br /><br /><strong>
  <em>Townsfolk knew to fear the monster coiled in the heart of the forest, who lured tourists with a cry that sounded like a woman weeping. Its fingers were sticks, its hair moss. It fed on sorrow and sowed corruption. You could lure it out with a singsong chant.</em>
</strong><br /><br />After, halfway through my read, I noticed a change in the ambience. Creepiness showed itself in the plot, through new characters and along with the turn of events; the prince had awoken and the city of Fairlord crept with wariness. It is since that moment that the plot upped in strangeness and…originality. I have no clue why it is the author chose to withhold the prince’s arisen for so long. Perhaps to possess more than enough time to include memories and solid background for our two main characters, Hazel and Ben? It was a wise thing to do, since it did make me understand both of their actions more – especially Ben whose tendency to go on date after date was worth questioning myself on what had unclenched it – but the limit was exceeded a little. It dragged.<br /><br /><em>
  <strong>Sometimes Ben told stories about how he would free the prince, with three magic words—words he’d never say out loud in front of Hazel. And in those stories, the prince was always villainous. Ben had to stop him before he destroyed Fairfold—and Ben did, through the power of love.</strong>
</em><br /><br />I had no idea there was going to be a gay main character in this standalone. It is not shelved as ‘LGBT’ but it should be, because it was an important part of the story. It may not have been a theme that shaded the importance of the others, but a theme nonetheless. I must say that, having read quite a few LGBT books and M/M romances in the past, I was not one hundred percent convinced regarding the two gay character’s (Ben + to-discover) love for each other, especially Ben’s. It very much felt like insta-love even though they technically knew each other for a long long time. But I must admit that it mostly was due to Ben’s easiness at falling in love that kept me from swoon-writhingly shipping the couple. Their shyness toward one another was sweet, but nothing more. Still, I am, most of the time, cheery when LGBT is included in a story, so I’m glad it was. Surely, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25422.Holly_Black" title="Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">Holly Black</a> could come to master the genre, if only she would explore it in more detail.<br /><br />While it did not impress me in any way, it was still an interesting enough and remotely mystical read, filled with fairies and magic. And in which the strong bond a brother and sister can share was present and beautiful.<br /><br />*I just remembered having read one of hers in the past: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20578940.The_Iron_Trial__Magisterium___1_" title="The Iron Trial (Magisterium, #1) by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">The Iron Trial</a>, a book she has co-written with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/150038.Cassandra_Clare" title="Cassandra Clare" rel="nofollow noopener">Cassandra Clare</a>. Yet, somehow, it slipped off my mind when writing the review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9558718422290167570" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_931439997" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/931439997" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/931439997?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Black's Modern Faerie series</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=coverly-love">coverly-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=paranormal-uf">paranormal-uf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer931439997" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17455770560218934546"><b>Oh book, you make it so difficult to rate you.</b><br/><br/>The thing about Holly Black is that she writes in very different styles. Before I read <i>White Cat</i>, I tried the first of her Faerie books - <i>Tithe</i> - (really didn't get into it), and her Spiderwick Chronicles (cute kids books but not really my thing). Then I discovered the Curse Workers trilogy and holy shit awesomeness: it was great! I liked the characters, the plot, and the twists... so much good.<br/><br/><i>The Darkest Part of the Forest</i> feels closer to her earli</span>
  <span id="freeText17455770560218934546" style="display:none"><b>Oh book, you make it so difficult to rate you.</b><br /><br />The thing about Holly Black is that she writes in very different styles. Before I read <i>White Cat</i>, I tried the first of her Faerie books - <i>Tithe</i> - (really didn't get into it), and her Spiderwick Chronicles (cute kids books but not really my thing). Then I discovered the Curse Workers trilogy and holy shit awesomeness: it was great! I liked the characters, the plot, and the twists... so much good.<br /><br /><i>The Darkest Part of the Forest</i> feels closer to her earlier works. There's something about her writing here that doesn't agree with me; that takes a premise that I was desperate to fall in love with... and makes it so very not compelling. I'm going to try and explain what it is the best I can, because when you strip this book down to what it plainly is, it should totally be my thing. It just isn't.<br /><br /><b>What is this book?</b><br />It's a dark, creepy fairy tale. I know what you're thinking: YEEESSSSS! I was too. It's about people who make deals with Fae folk and have to pay the price; it's about beautiful Fae princes who awaken after hundreds of years and wreak havoc; it's about the secrets that hide in the darkest part of the woods. <br /><br />Oh god... aren't you just desperate to get a load of that? If someone said those words to me about a book, I would be preordering it within an instant. But this book had a couple of intriguing first chapters with an interesting protagonist and promises of creepy, dark goodness, and then it became so difficult to read on. It felt like an effort to make myself pick the book back up. <br /><br />I'm not even sure if it is the writing itself that makes the plot so not compelling. Or if the plot sounds good but fails in the execution. All I know is that I never came to care what was going to happen. We were told that the situation was dire, but I never got a sense of that. The setting and language was creepy and atmospheric, but the main story wasn't. In fact, it seemed pretty juvenile.<br /><br />I would almost describe this as a Spiderwick Chronicles for older teens. A brother and sister must tackle the world of the Fae folk - a world that constantly introduces us to an assortment of creatures that I cannot even recall right now. Occasionally, we got really cool passages like this:<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“He couldn’t have understood what it felt like to dance until the force of his steps seemed to crack open the earth itself, to be among creatures who had never been human and could never be human, to be one of them. And Ben couldn’t have known the shame that Jack felt after, when, sweat cooling on his skin, he promised himself that when they came for him the next time, he wouldn’t go.<br />A promise that he’d never keep.”</i>
</b><br /><br />But the story just wasn't doing it for me. Plus, it was peppered with flashbacks that distracted me from the main issue at hand and didn't really add anything (most of them, anyway). <br /><br />This was one of my most highly anticipated releases - so disappointing.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.leafmarks.com/emilymay" rel="nofollow noopener">Leafmarks</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://mycountryheart.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17455770560218934546" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2193717747" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2193717747" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2193717747?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/22396077-the-darkest-part-of-the-forest">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2193717747" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1472929901749351826"><i>”They were in love with him because he was a prince and a faerie and magical and you were supposed to love princes and faeries and magic people."</i><br/><br/><u>
  <b>This LINE!!!</b>
</u> It resonated so much with me when I read the book! <br/>It describes my love for faeries in the best possible way and I can’t thank Holly Black enough for writing it down! I think this is going to be one of my favourite quotes ever. XD<br/>And I’m convinced Holly Black and I will have a very long and prosperous relationship in the future! If all </span>
  <span id="freeText1472929901749351826" style="display:none"><i>”They were in love with him because he was a prince and a faerie and magical and you were supposed to love princes and faeries and magic people."</i><br /><br /><u>
  <b>This LINE!!!</b>
</u> It resonated so much with me when I read the book! <br />It describes my love for faeries in the best possible way and I can’t thank Holly Black enough for writing it down! I think this is going to be one of my favourite quotes ever. XD<br />And I’m convinced Holly Black and I will have a very long and prosperous relationship in the future! If all her books are at least as good as this one, I’ll give her all my money without even thinking about it!!! *lol*<br /><br />This wasn’t only exactly what I <b>needed</b> but also everything I ever <b>wanted</b>!!!<br /><b>HELL!</b> It was what I craved for all my life!! <br /><br />I’m no fan of nice faeries, I want them to be heartless, seductive, brutal and dangerous!<br />For me it’s no Tinker Bell! Nope! *shakes head*<br />I want the real deal and how they are described in the myths and legends. <br />And boy, did Holly Black deliver! <br />So deliciously that I can’t help but sigh whenever I think about the book. *lol*<br />I mean she even pulled off the rhymes. &lt;333<br /><br /><i>”There’s a monster in our wood. <br />She’ll get you if you’re not good. <br />Drag you under leaves and sticks. <br />Punish you for all your tricks. <br />A nest of hair and gnawed bone. <br />You are never, ever coming…<br />home.”</i><br /><br />The way she executed everything was just amazing to read!!!<br /><br /><b>The plot:</b><br /><br />An entire town which is living in coexistence with the fair folk?! CHECK!<br />Cruel, cunning faeries that twist your every word?! CHECK!<br />Mysterious happenings!? CHECK!<br />A magical fairy tale with a bisexual gifted red head, a strong heroine, a gorgeous and cheeky changeling and a seductive sleeping faerie prince who lies in a glass coffin and causes trouble by waking up?! CHECK! CHECK! CHECK! <b>CHECK!!!</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>IT. WAS. SO. FREAKING. MARVELLOUS!!!</u>
</b><br /><br />Do I have to say more?!<br /><br />No?! <br />Then let’s go to my favourite part! The character’s section! ;-P<br /><br /><b>The characters:</b><br /><br /><u>
  <b>If you don’t want to be spoiled you have to stop now, because this is the part where I quote the book and talk about the characters and their development! So yeah, lots of spoilers in your near vicinity! You better tread carefully or you heed my warning and leave now. It’s up to you. ;-P</b>
</u><br /><br /><b>Hazel:</b><br /><br /><i>”The trick was not to let herself think about it too much. Anything that stopped her from thinking would do. Anything that kept her from pressing her hand against her chest to feel the thudding of her own heart and know that each beat was another moment lost.”</i><br /><br />I really liked that girl! She’s so kick-ass and amazing! I mean she’s turning into a faerie knight in the night and at day she’s just a normal girl! How awesome is that?! Since the Alderking always took her memories she doesn’t remember anything of it though, which really sucks if you ask me. But then again she’s an honest and righteous girl who only wants the best for her people and to say to be one of the Alderking’s knight’s doesn’t fit with her believes as “daylight Hazel” would certainly be putting it more than just lightly. Still, I loved that she always wanted to do the right thing and I hated to see her suffer so much. =( Despite all her bravado she was just a human girl and it made me so sad when her brother finally realised that too! &gt;_&lt;<br /><br /><i>”It was too much. But there was no one else, so it couldn’t be too much. It had to be exactly enough. It had to be what she could handle, and she had to handle it.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Once, there was a girl who vowed she would save everyone in the world, but forgot herself.”</i><br /><br /><b>Jack:</b><br /><br /><i>”He’d regretted not riding alongside them ever since they’d come on the first full-moon night. When he refused them a second time, it nearly broke his heart. The third time he was helpless to resist the call. He went, and after, he feared he could not summon up the strength to resist them again.”</i><br /><br />Oh what a precious bae! This poor boy really didn’t have it easy! I mean everyone in Fairfold knew he’s a changeling and to deal with that on a daily basis must have been so damn exhausting. I could understand his urge to be with his people and to escape his human life and I could also relate to him wanting to live that life nevertheless. Jack was living in both worlds and it was obvious that it tore him apart, especially when the people of his town began to blame him for everything that happened. To fight not only against the prejudices of the people in Fairfold BUT also against those of the Fair Folk hurt him more than he cared to admit and I really hope that he’ll get his “human life” at the side of Hazel! =) Heaven knows he deserves it! *lol*<br /><br /><i>”Your mom and I had a long talk about this last night,” he said. “As far as we’re concerned, the whole town can burn; what we care about is you.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Let me have this time being human,” he said. “Over and over you tell me that I will never be mortal, that the span of one human life is so short as to mean nothing. Fine, then let me have my human life. Let all the mortals I love die and blow away to dust. Let me have Nia for a mother and Charles for a father and Carter for my brother. Let me be Jack Gordon, and when I am done, when all is dust and ashes, I will return to you and learn how to be your son.”</i><br /><br /><b>Benjamin:</b><br /><br /><i>”I can’t change his nature, but I can give him the gift of our music. He will play music so sweet that no one will be able to think of anything else when they hear it, music that contains the magic of faerie. It will weight on him and it will change him and it will make him an artist, no matter what else he desires. Every child needs a tragedy to become truly interesting.”</i><br /><br />My heart bled so much for Ben! What a burden to be so gifted but to be unable to understand it. To fight yourself each and every second of your life, because you have a power that scares you and is so unnatural that no one else is able to help you to deal with it. When I read about him breaking his hand on purpose I didn’t just wince but also almost physically ached. My poor musicians heart! You can kill people in books and I’ll cry you a river but hurt a musicians hands or his instrument and I’m completely devastated!!! The artist in me just can’t handle it. &gt;_&lt; I felt Ben’s pain like it was my own and boy, did it hurt!! Please Holly whatever you do, don’t hurt musician’s in your fairy tales. Such scenes make me feel completely out of my depth! *lol*<br /><br /><i>”Gifted, when he played a tune on a xylophone that made their babysitter weep. Gifted, his sister called him, when he charmed faeries in the woods and saved her life. (And doomed it, too, maybe.) But what he could do scared him. He couldn’t control it.”</i><br /><i>”It has to stop,” he said. “I’ve got to stop. Somebody has to stop me.”</i><br /><br /><i>”We love until we do not. For us, love doesn’t fade gradually. It snaps like a branch bent too far.” To Ben, love was the flame in which he wanted to be reborn. He wanted to be remade by it.</i><br /><br /><b>Severin:</b><br /><br /><i>”He was crushingly, heart-stoppingly beautiful.”</i> <br /><br />Severin! *sighs* I loved that faerie boy to bits and pieces!!! Despite his rather tense situation he was still so playful and fun and I found myself enjoying every single moment he was mentioned! XD The story of how he ended up in the glass coffin was such a typical fairy tale and I relished every second of it. *lol* I really wish I could say more about Severin but writing this review I realised that we actually didn’t get to see a lot of him. Even though he was the centre of the story, he actually didn’t appear all too much in it, which is kind of funny but also so damn sad because I really would have loved to get to know him better. &gt;_&lt;<br /><br /><i>”I had no idea how long a single day could be. I didn’t know that the span of a single mortal life would seem interminable as I lay unmoving in that case. I didn’t know.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Benjamin,” Severin said, his voice dropping low. His face was inhumanly beautiful, his eyes as cold as the sky above the clouds, where the atmosphere is too thin to breathe. “I have heard every word you’ve ever said to me. Every honeyed, silver-tongued word.”</i><br /><br /><b>The relationships &amp; ships:</b><br /><br /><u>Hazel &amp; Jack:</u><br /><br /><i>”So what do I wear?”<br />His eyes lit with wickedness. For the first time that day, something had amused him. “Anything you like or nothing at all.”</i><br /><br />The chemistry between those two was so damn nice! Haha! I loved it when Jack showed his cheeky side and since Hazel is so badass she always knew how to handle him. XD (Even if she didn’t and got slightly insecure. *lol*) I think the revel they went to was one of the coolest things I ever read and I really want to go to one myself. =) I love the way they interacted with each other and I definitely ship them, I’m just really worried about how this is going to end. I mean yeah the book ended but we know that Hazel isn’t immortal and Jack is. So urgh… I can imagine their future and it’s already breaking my heart. &gt;_&lt;<br /><br /><i>”My life has always been a powder keg waiting for a match.”<br />“Well, hello, match,” Hazel said, pointing to herself with both thumbs, but she smiled as she did it, hoping to take the sting out of the words.</i><br /><br /><i>”She hadn’t known how solid he’d feel. She couldn’t have guessed how he’d run his hand over her back, lazily, as if he didn’t know how to stop touching her, or how she’d shiver when he did.”</i><br /><br /><u>Hazel &amp; Ben:</u><br /><br /><i>”Hazel never cried. She was forged from iron; she never broke. No one was tougher than his sister. The worst part was how quietly she wept, as if she’d taught herself how, as if she was so used to doing it that it had just become the way she cried.”</i><br /><br />I loved the way the relationship of those two siblings was portrayed. It was so damn realistic and it was obvious that they were really close! They both tried to protect each other but in the end they eventually had to realise that they made a huge mistake by keeping their secrets to themselves. The most beautiful thing about them however, was that they trusted each other blindly. They both knew they had secrets from each other but that didn’t change anything about their trust and bond! And this, my goodreads friends, is so very rare and lovely! &lt;3 <br /><br /><i>”You and your sister are very dear to each other. To show your regard, you give each other lovely bouquets of lies.”</i><br /><br /><i>”She leaned across the bed and hugged him with all the strength in her limbs, hugged him until her bones ached. But no matter how hard she hugged him, she knew it would never be enough.”</i><br /><br /><u>Ben &amp; Severin:</u><br /><br /><i>”What do you think you're doing, grabbing her like that?"<br />Severin slid a little closer, moving as lightly as a dancer. "Oh, you mean instead of grabbing you?"</i><br /><br />HA!! I shipped them from the very first moment they spoke with each other! *lol* Those two were just too much fun to watch, Severin my poor broken and sentimental faerie prince and Ben my precious bean that was so insecure and damaged. I adored how they got closer and began to trust each other and if there is one thing I didn’t like about this book, then it certainly was the fact that they didn’t get as much room as I wanted them to. XD I know it was necessary for the storyline, but damn, I’d have loved to read more scenes with both of them. =))) <br /><br /><i>”I love you,” Severin said, looking up, looking at nothing at all, his face exultant. “I love you like in the storybooks. I love you like in the ballads. I love you like a lightning bolt. I’ve loved you since the third month you came and spoke with me. I loved that you made me want to laugh. I loved the way you were kind and the way you would pause when you spoke, as though you were waiting for me to answer you. I love you and I am mocking no one when I kiss you, no one at all.”</i><br /><br />All told <b>“The Darkest Part of the Forest”</b> was a wonderful fairy tale that kept me reading even though I was supposed to stop. I severely suffered from the <b>“Just one more chapter illnesss”</b> and I enjoyed it so much that I can genuinely recommend it to everyone who likes dark faeries and a little bit of mystery. You won’t regret it! ;-)</span>
  <a data-text-id="1472929901749351826" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1761765969" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1761765969" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1761765969?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=gay-genre-fiction">gay-genre-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-relationships">favorite-relationships</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-faves2016">z-faves2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=trope-subversion">trope-subversion</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=sff-high-fantasy">sff-high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=setting-porn">setting-porn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=elle-recs-list">elle-recs-list</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=identity">identity</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1761765969" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9121761662325291217"><b>This book is about evil fairies and subverting genre expectations</b>. <br/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>SUBVERTING TROPES AND BLENDING BINARIES</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>It took me a long time to figure out why, exactly, this book captivated me so much. Yes, it's definitely a <i>solid</i> read, but what made this a five-star-favorite-book-ever read? I think in the long run what stood out to me was how <b>Holly Black sees the tropes of this story and avoids them.</b> Ben and Hazel are essentially a role-reversal of typical fantasy heroes. The boy is the one in </span>
  <span id="freeText9121761662325291217" style="display:none"><b>This book is about evil fairies and subverting genre expectations</b>. <br /><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>SUBVERTING TROPES AND BLENDING BINARIES</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />It took me a long time to figure out why, exactly, this book captivated me so much. Yes, it's definitely a <i>solid</i> read, but what made this a five-star-favorite-book-ever read? I think in the long run what stood out to me was how <b>Holly Black sees the tropes of this story and avoids them.</b> Ben and Hazel are essentially a role-reversal of typical fantasy heroes. The boy is the one in love with a fair prince in the woods, the girl is the lionheart fighting for their lives. <br /><br />I also liked that <i>The Darkest Part of the Forest</i> is so... <b>not heteronormative.</b> I don't know how to describe it any better than that - Holly Black has this casual approach towards writing lgbtq characters that works <i>perfectly</i>. The entire world blends gender and sexuality binaries into this map that rings so true. <br /><br />All that being said, you need to have proper expectations for her writing. Black writes characters and relationships that are <i>fucked up</i> and doesn't always care to tell the audience “hey, this isn't okay.” There's this vibe of evil, of hate, that she's not trying to get rid of. <br /><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>CHARACTERS YOU HATE AND LOVE</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Holly Black is very good at writing unlikeable protagonists, <b>characters you somewhat despise and somewhat love.</b> She risks making you hate her protagonists so that you'll love her protagonists and I <i>love</i> it. <br /><br /><i>The Darkest Part of the Forest</i> has four main protagonists, two point of view characters and two somewhat-love-interests. I love all of them, of course. Black is very good at making you empathize with characters you feel as if you should dislike. Severin, for example, reads like he <i>should</i> be a villain. But the audience gets to decide whether he truly is. <br /><br />Hazel, though, is especially my favorite. She does not fit into any boxes; she is <b>both the warrior archetype and a complex subversion of the warrior archetype.</b> I felt as if I had a feel for her twenty pages in, and I never did give up that love for her. <br /><br />I also somewhat adore the way Holly Black writes relationships. She is this odd mix between a cynic and a hopeless romantic and her romance writing comes off exactly that way. Both romance plots here (I won't spoil with who!!) are understated but well-built all the same. <br /><br />And of course, there's the <b>emphasis on sibling bonds.</b> Ben and Hazel's sibling relationship is intricate and interesting. <br /><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>TENSION, FEAR, AND CLAUSTROPHOBIA</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />Holly Black's writing is incredibly tense. You constantly feel as if you have to figure out what happens next. <br /><br />The environment is maybe one of my other favorite things about this book. Ben and Hazel's small town feels like another world, <b>a claustrophobic hideaway cut off from all being</b>. It makes a perfect setting, just eerie enough to make you feel on edge. She managed to make me feel small in comparison to this world, to this town, in a very visceral way. It's <i>so</i> engaging. <br /><br /><u>VERDICT:</u> This is one of my favorites and I REALLY recommend it to everyone. If morally ambiguous fairies in an eerie setting subverting genre expectations sounds like your shit, you need to pick this up.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435-elise-the-bookish-actress" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/girladamparrish" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9121761662325291217" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1053668825" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1053668825" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1053668825?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2020">read-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=best-of-2015">best-of-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=magical-fantasy">magical-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=audio-books">audio-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=reread">reread</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1053668825" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1233248611753716038"><b>[read 2 | may 2020]</b><br/>I have lost words. I am so wholly in love with this book; it's caught my imagination and my heartbeat and I just kept listening to the audio (a+ recommendation for the audio by the way) and thinking, <i>"how did I forget this book was my life favourite?"</i> I hadn't read it in 5 years and it hurts how much I'd forgotten! It is a work of complete art: mixing the best character emotional arcs I've read in ages with the whimsy and darkness of fairies tangling with modern worlds. Also i</span>
  <span id="freeText1233248611753716038" style="display:none"><b>[read 2 | may 2020]</b><br />I have lost words. I am so wholly in love with this book; it's caught my imagination and my heartbeat and I just kept listening to the audio (a+ recommendation for the audio by the way) and thinking, <i>"how did I forget this book was my life favourite?"</i> I hadn't read it in 5 years and it hurts how much I'd forgotten! It is a work of complete art: mixing the best character emotional arcs I've read in ages with the whimsy and darkness of fairies tangling with modern worlds. Also it begs for a sequel and my heart will forever have a hole in it dedicated to Ben and Hazel, to Severin and Jack. <br />I just!! This caught me.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I also forgot how deeply I love Ben and Severin? How Severin was about to <i>die</i> but he spent his last words telling Ben that he loved him and had loved him this whole time and that he wasn't embarrassing or childish or stupid for believing in true love. It exists. And here is Severin bleeding out on the floor to say so. Yeah I just-- I will be a wreck over this forever.<br /><br />And then Hazel and Jack?? Hazel who breaks hearts before they break hers, and Jack who doesn't believe he is owed anything and so tentatively accepts whatever he's dealt in this stolen human life. Who takes blame and loves his family and refuses to cave to his monstrous nature even though he is in love with the shine of fairy lust and love and wickedness. There is just JACK and then there is my heart. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I need to cram this book immediately into everyone's hands. But also just keep it close to myself. I think it explored so many topics so well, with careful love: like the accidental neglect of children, of how the "odd kids" at school can so easily take blame, about the different kinds of love, and how lying to the people who mean the most to you isn't protecting them. Hazel is my favourite dumbass gryffindor knight now and forever.<br /><br /><br /><b>[read 1 | January 2015]</b><br />I expected to like it after reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12813630.The_Coldest_Girl_in_Coldtown" title="The Coldest Girl in Coldtown by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">The Coldest Girl in Coldtown</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6087756.White_Cat__Curse_Workers___1_" title="White Cat (Curse Workers, #1) by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">White Cat</a> (which have quickly risen to my "favourite books" category. But adore it this much?! It was so beautiful, so powerful, so intriguing and fantastical and dark and bloody that...I just loved it. <br /><br />It's a magical story about Hazel and her brother, Ben, and their love for a horned boy cursed to sleep in a glass coffin. My words (silly useless words I'm trying to string together, here, pfft) do not convey how awesome this is. They live in Fairfold, which is absolutely embroiled in fairies. It's a tourist attraction but the locals know the fairies are real. There's mischief. There's unexplainable phenomenon (like the horned boy). People die. Just your average day in Fairfold.<br /><br />I absolutely adored Hazel. She's brave and unbeatable and really has no concept of defeat. She seemed almost Peter Panish to me...she was in the process of growing up, but was still entirely in love with her magical childhood. (She slayed monsters with her brother who has a magical curse/gift for music. Normal stuff, you know?) Ben was equally wonderful and even got a few chapters in his POV. He's older, but more quiet, more easily trodden on. Equally important are Jack and Carter...and Jack is a changeling. Because every family, when their child gets kidnapped by fairies, will demand their <i>real</i> child back and keep the changeling. Of course...the horned boy was just wrapped in delicious magical mystery.<br /><br />If the characters aren't gorgeous enough...the writing is beautiful. At 30% in on my kindle ARC I suddenly stopped and realised I loved this book so much it hurt. It has a bit of a bittersweet ending and I'm half sorry it's a standalone. Don't get me wrong, I love standalones...but...I could read an entire series of this town of Fairfold and Hazel, Ben, and Jack with ease. They all broke my heart a little. <br /><br /><blockquote>Come now, my child, if we were planning to harm you, do you think we'd be lurking here beside the path in the very darkest part of the forest? (Kenneth Patchen)</blockquote><br /><blockquote>"So, just another dull night in Fairfold, where everyone's a lunatic or an elf."</blockquote><br /><blockquote>
  <i>There's a monster in our wood<br />She'll get you if you're not good<br />Drag you under leaves and sticks<br />Punish you for all your tricks<br />A nest of hair and gnawed bone<br />You are never, ever coming...home. </i>
</blockquote><br /><blockquote>He was every bit as monstrously beautiful as he'd been. You could drown in beauty like that. </blockquote><br /><blockquote>It was disorientating to stumble along, aware that he might be taking her somewhere to kill her and at the same time, confusingly, embarrassed that he was going to kill her while she was wearing pajamas and wellies. If she'd known she was going to die at his hand, she would have dressed up. </blockquote><br /><blockquote>"I am no hob or hearth spirit, to be obligated by gifts."<br />"We weren't trying to obligate you," she said. "We were trying to be nice."<br />The horned boy bowed his head slightly, a thin smile on his face that she thought might be self-disgust. "You may call me Severin," he said. "Now we are both nice." </blockquote><br /><blockquote>Once normal had been a heavy, smothering blanket she feared being trapped beneath. But now normal felt fragile, as though she could unravel it just by teasing a single string. </blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="1233248611753716038" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="booksnpenguins" class="user" itemprop="url" name="booksnpenguins" href="/user/show/66222749-booksnpenguins">booksnpenguins</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/22396077-the-darkest-part-of-the-forest">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66222749-booksnpenguins?shelf=royal-binches">royal-binches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66222749-booksnpenguins?shelf=shippity-ship-ship">shippity-ship-ship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66222749-booksnpenguins?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66222749-booksnpenguins?shelf=fae-and-fairies">fae-and-fairies</a>
